## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of concentration change dA/dt as a function of time t and concentration A, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics — determining the rate law. The presence of both t and A as features suggests either a non-elementary rate law, a coupled reaction system where other species have been eliminated in terms of t, or time-dependent reaction conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions with equilibrium)
- Reversible second-order/first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate expression from coupled equilibria)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (product-catalyzed reaction, logistic-type kinetics)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with time-dependent effective rate constant)
- Coupled system elimination: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (rate depending on another species expressed via its time solution)
- Consecutive reaction effective rate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (from multi-step sequential reactions)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (substrate inhibition or saturation kinetics without enzyme notation)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (rate with substrate inhibition at high concentration)
- Mixed time-concentration: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (empirical power-law in both time and concentration)
- Damped oscillatory rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * cos(c1 * t + c2) (oscillatory reaction systems like BZ reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → classical rate law dA/dt = k*A^n; if t appears, the system likely involves coupled species or external forcing
- Linear dependence on A with nonzero intercept → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium, dA/dt = k_f*(A_eq - A) form
- Exponential terms in t → other species in a coupled reaction network have been analytically solved and substituted
- Quadratic or higher polynomial in A → multi-molecular reaction steps or autocatalytic mechanisms
- Rational functions of A (saturation form) → enzyme-like catalysis or surface-mediated reactions with limited active sites
- Product of A and (1-A/c) → logistic/autocatalytic kinetics with a carrying capacity or stoichiometric constraint
- Sign of leading coefficient indicates consumption (negative) vs production (positive) of species A
- Fractional power of A (e.g., A**0.5) → chain reaction mechanisms where radical intermediates are in quasi-steady state
